\hypertarget{pdb_8h_ad77422fc2b983565a6a18f7637b90ccb}{\index{pdb.\-h@{pdb.\-h}!bl\-Atom\-Name\-Match@{bl\-Atom\-Name\-Match}}
\index{bl\-Atom\-Name\-Match@{bl\-Atom\-Name\-Match}!pdb.h@{pdb.\-h}}
\subsubsection[{bl\-Atom\-Name\-Match}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf B\-O\-O\-L} bl\-Atom\-Name\-Match (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{char $\ast$}]{atnam, }
\item[{char $\ast$}]{spec, }
\item[{{\bf B\-O\-O\-L} $\ast$}]{Error\-Warn}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}\label{pdb_8h_ad77422fc2b983565a6a18f7637b90ccb}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$atnam} & The atom name to test \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$spec} & The atom specification \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt in,out}  & {\em $\ast$\-Error\-Warn} & On input, if T\-R\-U\-E, this routine will indicate errors. On output, indicates whether there was an error. Note that you must be careful to supply an lvalue here, you can't just use T\-R\-U\-E or F\-A\-L\-S\-E since it's modified on return. N\-U\-L\-L is allowed if you don't care about errors.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
Tests whether an atom name matches an atom name specification. ? or \% is used to match a single character is used to match any trailing characters; it may not be used for leading characters or in the middle of a specification (e.\-g. {\itshape B}, C$\ast$2 are both illegal). Wildcards may be escaped with a backslash.

For example\-: C$\ast$ matches all carbon atoms, O5$\ast$ matches an atom called O5$\ast$ ?B$\ast$ matches all beta atoms


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item 23.\-07.\-96 Original By\-: A\-C\-R\-M
\item 07.\-07.\-14 Use bl prefix for functions By\-: C\-T\-P 
\end{DoxyItemize}

Definition at line 139 of file Atom\-Name\-Match.\-c.

\hypertarget{pdb_8h_ad421ee2a06f5464d432a05ca77f3816e}{\index{pdb.\-h@{pdb.\-h}!bl\-Atom\-Name\-Raw\-Match@{bl\-Atom\-Name\-Raw\-Match}}
\index{bl\-Atom\-Name\-Raw\-Match@{bl\-Atom\-Name\-Raw\-Match}!pdb.h@{pdb.\-h}}
\subsubsection[{bl\-Atom\-Name\-Raw\-Match}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf B\-O\-O\-L} bl\-Atom\-Name\-Raw\-Match (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{char $\ast$}]{atnam, }
\item[{char $\ast$}]{spec, }
\item[{{\bf B\-O\-O\-L} $\ast$}]{Error\-Warn}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}\label{pdb_8h_ad421ee2a06f5464d432a05ca77f3816e}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$atnam} & The atom name to check \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$spec} & The atom specification \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt in,out}  & {\em $\ast$\-Error\-Warn} & On input, if T\-R\-U\-E, this routine will indicate errors. On output, indicates whether there was an error. Note that you must be careful to supply an lvalue here, you can't just use T\-R\-U\-E or F\-A\-L\-S\-E since it's modified on return. N\-U\-L\-L is allowed if you don't care about errors.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
Tests whether an atom name matches an atom name specification.

This version should be given the raw atom name rather than the massaged one. i.\-e. \char`\"{} C\-A \char`\"{} is C-\/alpha, \char`\"{}\-C\-A  \char`\"{} is Calcium

Normally it checks against the second character onwards unless the spec starts with a $<$ in which case it checks from the beginning of the string

Written as a wrapper to Atom\-Name\-Match()

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}

\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Were all C\-O\-N\-E\-C\-Ts added O\-K
\end{DoxyReturn}
Deletes all current connectivity data and rebuilds it using covalent radii data. A return of F\-A\-L\-S\-E indicates that there were too many connections for an atom. If this happens, M\-A\-X\-C\-O\-N\-E\-C\-T needs to be increased in \hyperlink{pdb_8h}{pdb.\-h}

\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em type} & Torsion type (see below) \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Torsion angle
\end{DoxyReturn}
Calculates a sidechain torsion angle from a pdb linked list. The atoms to be included in the calculation are specified by type.

\begin{DoxyVerb}     type     Atom names        Sequential atom numbers
     --------------------------------------------------
     0        N,  CA, CB, XG    (0 - 1 - 4 - 5)
     1        CA, CB, XG, XD    (1 - 4 - 5 - 6)
     2        CB, XG, XD, XE    (4 - 5 - 6 - 7)
     3        XG, XD, XE, XZ    (5 - 6 - 7 - 8)
\end{DoxyVerb}

\hypertarget{pdb_8h_a6ebc5a7fce0f1a2d8057fea055c99b6a}{\index{pdb.\-h@{pdb.\-h}!bl\-Do\-Parse\-Res\-Spec@{bl\-Do\-Parse\-Res\-Spec}}
\index{bl\-Do\-Parse\-Res\-Spec@{bl\-Do\-Parse\-Res\-Spec}!pdb.h@{pdb.\-h}}
\subsubsection[{bl\-Do\-Parse\-Res\-Spec}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf B\-O\-O\-L} bl\-Do\-Parse\-Res\-Spec (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{char $\ast$}]{in\-Spec, }
\item[{char $\ast$}]{chain, }
\item[{int $\ast$}]{resnum, }
\item[{char $\ast$}]{insert, }
\item[{{\bf B\-O\-O\-L}}]{uppercaseresspec}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}\label{pdb_8h_a6ebc5a7fce0f1a2d8057fea055c99b6a}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$in\-Spec} & Residue specification \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt out}  & {\em $\ast$chain} & Chain label \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt out}  & {\em $\ast$resnum} & Residue number \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt out}  & {\em $\ast$insert} & Insert label \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em uppercaseresspec} & Convert spec to upper case. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Success?
\end{DoxyReturn}
Note that chain and insert must be arrays of at least 2 characters, not character pointers

Splits up a residue specification of the form \mbox{[}c\mbox{]}\mbox{[}.\mbox{]}num\mbox{[}i\mbox{]} into chain, resnum and insert. Chain and insert are optional and will be set to spaces if not specified. If uppercaseresspec equals T\-R\-U\-E, the spec is upper cased before processing

Multi-\/letter chain I\-Ds can be parsed. Additionally, chain I\-Ds with numerical characters can be parsed if a period is used to separate the chain from the residue number.

\item 17.\-07.\-95 Added B\-O\-O\-L return
\item 18.\-03.\-98 Added option to include a . to separate chain and residue number so numeric chain names can be used
\item 29.\-09.\-05 Moved this code to from Parse\-Res\-Spec() to Do\-Parse\-Res\-Spec() and made that function just call this new function. This move is to allow this underlying function to have an extra parameter to specify whether or not the residue specification should be upper cased (without affecting code that calls the old function). By\-: T\-L

\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$fpin} & A pointer to type F\-I\-L\-E in which the .P\-D\-B file is stored. \\

\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em All\-Atoms} & T\-R\-U\-E\-: A\-T\-O\-M \& H\-E\-T\-A\-T\-M records F\-A\-L\-S\-E\-: A\-T\-O\-M records only \\

\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A pointer to a malloc'd W\-H\-O\-L\-E\-P\-D\-B structure.
\end{DoxyReturn}
Reads a P\-D\-B\-M\-L-\/formatted P\-D\-B file into a P\-D\-B linked list.

The Occ\-Rank value indicates occupancy ranking to read for partial occupancy atoms. If any partial occupancy atoms are read the global flag g\-P\-D\-B\-Partial\-Occ is set to T\-R\-U\-E.

The global multiple-\/models flag is set to true if more than one model is found.

Returns N\-U\-L\-L if memory allocation fails or returns wpdb with wpdb-\/$>$pdb set to N\-U\-L\-L and wpdb-\/$>$natoms set to -\/1.

P\-D\-B linked list of the region of interest.
\end{DoxyReturn}
Reduces a P\-D\-B linked list to those residues within a specified zone. Note that the P\-D\-B linked list is duplicated before extraction so pointers do not match those in the input P\-D\-B linked list. Excess records in the new P\-D\-B linked list are freed.

\item 22.\-03.\-06 Modified to allow non-\/exact zones. i.\-e. the extracted zone will be the widest subset of the specified zone. So, if you specifiy 30-\/35\-Z and the P\-D\-B file only has 30-\/35\-B then that will be extracted.
\item 29.\-10.\-10 Fixed extraction where end of zone matched last residue in a chain

\hline
\mbox{\tt out}  & {\em rm} & Rotation matrix \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Success
\end{DoxyReturn}
Does a weigthed fitting of 2 P\-D\-B linked lists. The C\-A and C\-B are given a weight of 1.\-0 while the other atoms are given a weight of 1.\-0/natom in the residue. Thus for N,C\-A,C,C\-B backbone only, this will be N and C with weights of 0.\-25

\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Fixed atom name (pointer into name)
\end{DoxyReturn}
Fixes an atom name by removing leading spaces, or moving a leading digit to the end of the string. Used by do\-Read\-P\-D\-B()


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item 06.\-04.\-94 Original By\-: A\-C\-R\-M
\item 01.\-03.\-01 No longer static
\item 03.\-06.\-05 The name passed in has always contained the column which is officially the alternate atom position indicator, but is used by some programs as part of the atom name. Thus the properly constructed variable coming into the routine should be something like '1\-H\-G1 ' or '1\-H\-G1\-A' for an alternate atom position. However some programs use ' H\-G11'. Therefore we now check for a character in the last position and replace it with a space if there is a space in the preceeding position (e.\-g. ' C\-A A' -\/$>$ ' C\-A ') or if there is a character in the first position (e.\-g. '1\-H\-G1\-A' -\/$>$ '1\-H\-G1 ') or if the occupancy is not zero/one N\-O\-T\-E!!! To support this, the routine now has a second parameter\-: R\-E\-A\-L occup
\item 07.\-07.\-14 Renamed to \hyperlink{pdb_8h_a4beae504260cb072d1807d1e3aaa1982}{bl\-Fix\-Atom\-Name()} By\-: C\-T\-P 
\end{DoxyItemize}

Definition at line 1294 of file Read\-P\-D\-B.\-c.

\hypertarget{pdb_8h_a906f5c2c60e2384016857f256b060bca}{\index{pdb.\-h@{pdb.\-h}!bl\-Fix\-Order\-P\-D\-B@{bl\-Fix\-Order\-P\-D\-B}}
\index{bl\-Fix\-Order\-P\-D\-B@{bl\-Fix\-Order\-P\-D\-B}!pdb.h@{pdb.\-h}}
\subsubsection[{bl\-Fix\-Order\-P\-D\-B}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf P\-D\-B}$\ast$ bl\-Fix\-Order\-P\-D\-B (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf P\-D\-B} $\ast$}]{pdb, }

\item[{{\bf B\-O\-O\-L}}]{Renum}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}\label{pdb_8h_a906f5c2c60e2384016857f256b060bca}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$pdb} & P\-D\-B linked list to fix atom order \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em Pad} & T\-R\-U\-E\-: Create dummy coordinate atoms for any missing atoms in standard residues \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em Renum} & T\-R\-U\-E\-: Renumber the atoms \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Corrected P\-D\-B linked list
\end{DoxyReturn}
Runs through a P\-D\-B linked list and corrects the atom order to match the N,C\-A,C,O,s/c standard. Only standard amino acids are processed. The input linked list is modified (i.\-e. a new list is not built), but the return value from the routine should be used for the corrected list rather than the input P\-D\-B pointer, since the start of the list may have changed. i.\-e. the routine should be called with the form\-: \begin{DoxyVerb}           pdb = FixOrderPDB(pdb,TRUE,TRUE);
\end{DoxyVerb}



\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item 08.\-07.\-93 Original By\-: A\-C\-R\-M

\hypertarget{pdb_8h_aacdc4e74b6ceab09f8f19a09a0820b26}{\index{pdb.\-h@{pdb.\-h}!bl\-F\-Nam2\-P\-D\-B@{bl\-F\-Nam2\-P\-D\-B}}
\index{bl\-F\-Nam2\-P\-D\-B@{bl\-F\-Nam2\-P\-D\-B}!pdb.h@{pdb.\-h}}
\subsubsection[{bl\-F\-Nam2\-P\-D\-B}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}char$\ast$ bl\-F\-Nam2\-P\-D\-B (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{char $\ast$}]{filename}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}\label{pdb_8h_aacdc4e74b6ceab09f8f19a09a0820b26}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$filename} & A P\-D\-B filename containing a P\-D\-B code \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
The P\-D\-B code (lower case) N\-U\-L\-L if memory allocation fails X\-X\-X\-X if filename blank or N\-U\-L\-L or if unable to find P\-D\-B code
\end{DoxyReturn}
This routine attempts to convert a filename stem to a P\-D\-B code.

All the following inputs should produce the same output of 1fbj\-:

\begin{DoxyVerb}  $A:[PDB]PDB1FBJ.ENT
  C:\P1FBJ.PDB
  /pdb/p1fbj.pdb
  /pdb/pdb1fbj.pdb
  1fbj.pdb
  1fbjL
\end{DoxyVerb}


The routine first removes characters from the start of the filename up to the last \-: \mbox{]} / or . It then searches for the following possible patterns (where N is a digit and X is an alphanumeric)

\begin{DoxyVerb}  pdbNXXX
  pNXXX
  NXXX
  XXXX.pdb
  XXXX.ent
\end{DoxyVerb}


This should cover just about any filename which includes a legal P\-D\-B code.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item 24.\-07.\-95 Original By\-: A\-C\-R\-M
\item 26.\-07.\-95 Corrected a N\-U\-L\-L to '\textbackslash{}0'
\item 07.\-07.\-14 Use bl prefix for functions By\-: C\-T\-P 
\end{DoxyItemize}

Definition at line 123 of file F\-Nam2\-P\-D\-B.\-c.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
P\-D\-B linked list of the region of interest.
\end{DoxyReturn}
Reduces a P\-D\-B linked list to those residues outside a specified zone. Note that the P\-D\-B linked list is duplicated before extraction so pointers do not match those in the input P\-D\-B linked list. Excess records in the new P\-D\-B linked list are freed.

Forces extraction even if the zone residues are not found

N\-O\-T\-E\-: if neither residue is found, the whole linked list will be returned.

\hypertarget{pdb_8h_a92e5b91f6d1c9fce21d9f2b0060c36b0}{\index{pdb.\-h@{pdb.\-h}!bl\-Get\-Biomolecule\-Whole\-P\-D\-B@{bl\-Get\-Biomolecule\-Whole\-P\-D\-B}}
\index{bl\-Get\-Biomolecule\-Whole\-P\-D\-B@{bl\-Get\-Biomolecule\-Whole\-P\-D\-B}!pdb.h@{pdb.\-h}}
\subsubsection[{bl\-Get\-Biomolecule\-Whole\-P\-D\-B}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf B\-I\-O\-M\-O\-L\-E\-C\-U\-L\-E}$\ast$ bl\-Get\-Biomolecule\-Whole\-P\-D\-B (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf W\-H\-O\-L\-E\-P\-D\-B} $\ast$}]{wpdb}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}\label{pdb_8h_a92e5b91f6d1c9fce21d9f2b0060c36b0}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$wpdb} & Pointer to W\-H\-O\-L\-E\-P\-D\-B structure \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Pointer to malloc()'d B\-I\-O\-M\-O\-L\-E\-C\-U\-L\-E linked list
\end{DoxyReturn}
Reads the biomolecule assembly data from R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 300 and R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 350 headers.

The returned pointer is a linked list of B\-I\-O\-M\-O\-L\-E\-C\-U\-L\-E structures. The first item in the list contains the information from R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 300\-: the total number of biomolecule assemblies and any additional information provided in R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 300 beyond the standard comments. The additional information (biomolecule-\/$>$details) is a S\-T\-R\-I\-N\-G\-L\-I\-S\-T linked list.

The list of chains will appear in biomolcule-\/$>$chains as a comma separated list and the transformation to be applied to them will appear in the biomolecule-\/$>$biomt structure. This is also a linked list so if multiple transformations are required these will appear in further entries to this list.

Additional entries will be found in the B\-I\-O\-M\-O\-L\-E\-C\-U\-L\-E linked list for each different biomolecule.

See the test code in \hyperlink{_p_d_b_header_info_8c}{P\-D\-B\-Header\-Info.\-c} for example usage.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item 26.\-06.\-15 Original By\-: A\-C\-R\-M 
\end{DoxyItemize}

Read the crystal parameters (unit cell, spacegroup, origin and scale matrices) out of a P\-D\-B file.

Stops searching as soon as an A\-T\-O\-M or H\-E\-T\-A\-T\-M record is hit and leaves the file in a state ready for Read\-P\-D\-B() to do it's stuff (i.\-e. with the current file pointer at the first A\-T\-O\-M or H\-E\-T\-A\-T\-M record).

\index{bl\-Get\-Exptl\-Old@{bl\-Get\-Exptl\-Old}!pdb.h@{pdb.\-h}}
\subsubsection[{bl\-Get\-Exptl\-Old}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf B\-O\-O\-L} bl\-Get\-Exptl\-Old (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{F\-I\-L\-E $\ast$}]{fp, }
\item[{{\bf R\-E\-A\-L} $\ast$}]{resolution, }
\item[{{\bf R\-E\-A\-L} $\ast$}]{R\-Factor, }
\item[{{\bf R\-E\-A\-L} $\ast$}]{Free\-R, }
\item[{int $\ast$}]{Struc\-Type}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}\label{pdb_8h_a09f6999081df2204ee322f785319282e}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$fp} & P\-D\-B file pointer \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt out}  & {\em $\ast$resolution} & The resolution (0.\-0 if not applicable) \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt out}  & {\em $\ast$\-R\-Factor} & The R-\/factor (0.\-0 if not found) \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt out}  & {\em $\ast$\-Free\-R} & The Free R-\/factor (0.\-0 if not found) \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt out}  & {\em $\ast$\-Struc\-Type} & Structure type\-: S\-T\-R\-U\-C\-T\-U\-R\-E\-\_\-\-T\-Y\-P\-E\-\_\-\-X\-T\-A\-L S\-T\-R\-U\-C\-T\-U\-R\-E\-\_\-\-T\-Y\-P\-E\-\_\-\-N\-M\-R S\-T\-R\-U\-C\-T\-U\-R\-E\-\_\-\-T\-Y\-P\-E\-\_\-\-M\-O\-D\-E\-L S\-T\-R\-U\-C\-T\-U\-R\-E\-\_\-\-T\-Y\-P\-E\-\_\-\-U\-N\-K\-N\-O\-W\-N \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
T\-R\-U\-E if resolution found (even if not applicable)
\end{DoxyReturn}
This routine attempts to obtain resolution and R-\/factor information out of a P\-D\-B file. It returns T\-R\-U\-E or F\-A\-L\-S\-E to indicate whether valid information was found. Resolution-\/not-\/applicable structures then have the resolution set to zero.

N.\-B. The resolution information returned by the routine is reliable; the R-\/factor information is stored in so many forms that it is difficult to read without some form of natural language parsing, but we manage to handle most situations. The routine assumes the R-\/factor to be the first number after the words `\-R-\/value' (or one of the other keys -\/ see the case statement in the code for the valid keywords). Thus we cannot handle records of the form\-: T\-H\-E R-\/\-V\-A\-L\-U\-E F\-O\-R 7142 R\-E\-F\-L\-E\-C\-T\-I\-O\-N\-S B\-E\-T\-W\-E\-E\-N 10.\-0 A\-N\-D 1.\-97 A\-N\-G\-S\-T\-R\-O\-M\-S R\-E\-F\-I\-N\-E\-M\-E\-N\-T C\-Y\-C\-L\-E 73 I\-S 0.\-254. as appears in entries such as 1\-L\-Z\-T. Here, the first number is the number of reflections. There is thus a kludge which sets the R-\/factor to zero if it was read as greater than 0.\-5 to avoid this situation. In these cases, we lose the R-\/factor information. This occurs in approx 3.\-5\% of the 1\-X\-X\-X P\-D\-B entries.

\item 25.\-02.\-94 Original By\-: A\-C\-R\-M
\item 28.\-02.\-94 Added \char`\"{} R = \char`\"{} and check that V\-A\-L\-U\-E wasn't B-\/\-V\-A\-L\-U\-E

\item 27.\-06.\-97 Added handing of R\-E\-S\-O\-L\-U\-T\-I\-O\-N records which point you to another record for the experiment type. Fixed some calls to Find\-Next\-Number() which were checking an 80 character width Fixed E\-X\-P\-E\-R\-I\-M\-E\-N\-T T\-Y\-P\-E to look for N\-M\-R as well Looks for E\-X\-P\-D\-T\-A N\-M\-R record
\item 23.\-03.\-98 Added check that R\-E\-S\-O\-L\-U\-T\-I\-O\-N record is in a R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 2
\item 08.\-03.\-99 Renamed to Get\-Exptl() from Get\-Resol\-P\-D\-B() and added Free\-R parameter. Get\-Resol\-P\-D\-B() is now a wrapper to this routine. Added additional pass which looks for the structured R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 3 records

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}

This routine attempts to obtain resolution and R-\/factor information out of a P\-D\-B file. It returns T\-R\-U\-E or F\-A\-L\-S\-E to indicate whether valid information was found. Resolution-\/not-\/applicable structures then have the resolution set to zero.

N.\-B. The resolution information returned by the routine is reliable; the R-\/factor information is stored in so many forms that it is difficult to read without some form of natural language parsing, but we manage to handle most situations. The routine assumes the R-\/factor to be the first number after the words `\-R-\/value' (or one of the other keys -\/ see the case statement in the code for the valid keywords). Thus we cannot handle records of the form\-: T\-H\-E R-\/\-V\-A\-L\-U\-E F\-O\-R 7142 R\-E\-F\-L\-E\-C\-T\-I\-O\-N\-S B\-E\-T\-W\-E\-E\-N 10.\-0 A\-N\-D 1.\-97 A\-N\-G\-S\-T\-R\-O\-M\-S R\-E\-F\-I\-N\-E\-M\-E\-N\-T C\-Y\-C\-L\-E 73 I\-S 0.\-254. as appears in entries such as 1\-L\-Z\-T. Here, the first number is the number of reflections. There is thus a kludge which sets the R-\/factor to zero if it was read as greater than 0.\-5 to avoid this situation. In these cases, we lose the R-\/factor information. This occurs in approx 3.\-5\% of the 1\-X\-X\-X P\-D\-B entries.

\hypertarget{pdb_8h_a4d5b4d6154f9efed0b1bf00dcb5aa16b}{\index{pdb.\-h@{pdb.\-h}!bl\-Get\-Resol\-Whole\-P\-D\-B@{bl\-Get\-Resol\-Whole\-P\-D\-B}}
\index{bl\-Get\-Resol\-Whole\-P\-D\-B@{bl\-Get\-Resol\-Whole\-P\-D\-B}!pdb.h@{pdb.\-h}}
\subsubsection[{bl\-Get\-Resol\-Whole\-P\-D\-B}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf B\-O\-O\-L} bl\-Get\-Resol\-Whole\-P\-D\-B (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf W\-H\-O\-L\-E\-P\-D\-B} $\ast$}]{wpdb, }
\item[{{\bf R\-E\-A\-L} $\ast$}]{resolution, }
\item[{{\bf R\-E\-A\-L} $\ast$}]{R\-Factor, }
\item[{int $\ast$}]{Struc\-Type}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}\label{pdb_8h_a4d5b4d6154f9efed0b1bf00dcb5aa16b}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$wpdb} & W\-H\-O\-L\-E\-P\-D\-B structure pointer \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt out}  & {\em $\ast$resolution} & The resolution (0.\-0 if not applicable) \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt out}  & {\em $\ast$\-R\-Factor} & The R-\/factor (0.\-0 if not found) \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt out}  & {\em $\ast$\-Struc\-Type} & Structure type\-: S\-T\-R\-U\-C\-T\-U\-R\-E\-\_\-\-T\-Y\-P\-E\-\_\-\-X\-T\-A\-L S\-T\-R\-U\-C\-T\-U\-R\-E\-\_\-\-T\-Y\-P\-E\-\_\-\-N\-M\-R S\-T\-R\-U\-C\-T\-U\-R\-E\-\_\-\-T\-Y\-P\-E\-\_\-\-M\-O\-D\-E\-L S\-T\-R\-U\-C\-T\-U\-R\-E\-\_\-\-T\-Y\-P\-E\-\_\-\-U\-N\-K\-N\-O\-W\-N \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
T\-R\-U\-E if resolution found or valid structure type found
\end{DoxyReturn}
This routine attempts to obtain resolution and R-\/factor information out of a W\-H\-O\-L\-E\-P\-D\-B structure. It returns T\-R\-U\-E or F\-A\-L\-S\-E to indicate whether valid information was found. Resolution-\/not-\/applicable structures then have the resolution set to zero.

N.\-B. The resolution information returned by the routine is reliable; the R-\/factor information is stored in so many forms that it is difficult to read without some form of natural language parsing, but we manage to handle most situations. The routine assumes the R-\/factor to be the first number after the words `\-R-\/value' (or one of the other keys -\/ see the case statement in the code for the valid keywords). Thus we cannot handle records of the form\-: T\-H\-E R-\/\-V\-A\-L\-U\-E F\-O\-R 7142 R\-E\-F\-L\-E\-C\-T\-I\-O\-N\-S B\-E\-T\-W\-E\-E\-N 10.\-0 A\-N\-D 1.\-97 A\-N\-G\-S\-T\-R\-O\-M\-S R\-E\-F\-I\-N\-E\-M\-E\-N\-T C\-Y\-C\-L\-E 73 I\-S 0.\-254. as appears in entries such as 1\-L\-Z\-T. Here, the first number is the number of reflections. There is thus a kludge which sets the R-\/factor to zero if it was read as greater than 0.\-5 to avoid this situation. In these cases, we lose the R-\/factor information. This occurs in approx 3.\-5\% of the 1\-X\-X\-X P\-D\-B entries.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item 02.\-03.\-15 Original By\-: A\-C\-R\-M 
\end{DoxyItemize}

Definition at line 244 of file Resol\-P\-D\-B.\-c.

Globals\-: \hyperlink{struct_h_a_d_d_i_n_f_o}{H\-A\-D\-D\-I\-N\-F\-O} g\-Hadd\-Info Information on Hs added

This routine adds hydrogens to a P\-D\-B linked list. Performs all necessary functions.

N.\-B. Because of the variation in styles required for N-\/terminal Hs, this routine adds {\itshape no} hydrogens to the N-\/terminal residue. Fix\-P\-D\-B() may be used for this purpose if C\-H\-A\-R\-M\-M/\-C\-O\-N\-G\-E\-N style hydrogens are required.

\hypertarget{pdb_8h_ae13d973e92945be6cc5de8fad4bccc3a}{\index{pdb.\-h@{pdb.\-h}!bl\-Parse\-Res\-Spec@{bl\-Parse\-Res\-Spec}}
\index{bl\-Parse\-Res\-Spec@{bl\-Parse\-Res\-Spec}!pdb.h@{pdb.\-h}}
\subsubsection[{bl\-Parse\-Res\-Spec}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf B\-O\-O\-L} bl\-Parse\-Res\-Spec (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{char $\ast$}]{spec, }
\item[{char $\ast$}]{chain, }
\item[{int $\ast$}]{resnum, }
\item[{char $\ast$}]{insert}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}\label{pdb_8h_ae13d973e92945be6cc5de8fad4bccc3a}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$spec} & Residue specification \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt out}  & {\em $\ast$chain} & Chain label \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt out}  & {\em $\ast$resnum} & Residue number \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt out}  & {\em $\ast$insert} & Insert label \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Success?
\end{DoxyReturn}
Note that chain and insert must be arrays of at least 2 characters, not character pointers

Splits up a residue specification of the form \mbox{[}c\mbox{]}\mbox{[}.\mbox{]}num\mbox{[}i\mbox{]} into chain, resnum and insert. Chain and insert are optional and will be set to spaces if not specified. Converts the resiude specification to upper case before processing.

Moved the code that was here to a new function, Do\-Parse\-Res\-Spec() and made this function just call that new function. See Do\-Parse\-Res\-Spec()'s comments for notes on previous changes. This move is to allow the underlying function to have an extra parameter to specify whether or not the residue specification should be upper cased (without affecting code that calls this function).


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item 29.\-09.\-05 Original By\-: T\-L
\item 05.\-01.\-12 Now behaves the same as Parse\-Res\-Spec\-No\-Upper(). There are now too many P\-D\-B files with lower case chain names (e.\-g. 1gav, 3n9r, etc.) for the old default behaviour or up-\/casing everything. By\-: A\-C\-R\-M
\item 07.\-07.\-14 Use bl prefix for functions By\-: C\-T\-P 
\end{DoxyItemize}

Definition at line 158 of file Parse\-Res.\-c.

Number of parameters read. (0 on error)
\end{DoxyReturn}
Read a proton generation parameter file. All data are placed in static arrays used by the hydrogen adding routines. Normally this routine is only called by the first call to H\-Add\-P\-D\-B(). It is only necessary to call this routine explicitly if the P\-G\-P file is changed between calls to H\-Add\-P\-D\-B() and thus needs re-\/reading.

\end{DoxyReturn}
Reads secondary structure information from the header of a P\-D\-B file. Returns a pointer to a linked list of type S\-E\-C\-S\-T\-R\-U\-C.

On return, the variable nsec, or the value returned by the routine should be checked to ensure some secondary structure was returned. The secondary structure is stored together with ranges of residues to which it applies. The form of the structure should be checked in \hyperlink{pdb_8h}{pdb.\-h}

Reads the sequence from the S\-E\-Q\-R\-E\-S records of a P\-D\-B file. Creates an array of malloc()'d character arrays in which the sequence is stored. Can therefore cope with any size of sequence information from the P\-D\-B file.

This is not normally recommended to get the sequence for a P\-D\-B file this way, but is useful to detect discrepancies compared with the sequence described by the A\-T\-O\-M records.

Coordinate data is accessed as linked list of type P\-D\-B as follows\-:

W\-H\-O\-L\-E\-P\-D\-B $\ast$wpdb; P\-D\-B $\ast$p; wpdb = Read\-Whole\-P\-D\-B(fp); for(p=wpdb-\/$>$pdb; p!=N\-U\-L\-L; p=p-\/$>$next) \{ ... Do something with p ... \}

\hypertarget{pdb_8h_af900f21c1a37ba63496962ab1ffec576}{\index{pdb.\-h@{pdb.\-h}!bl\-Rep\-One\-S\-Chain@{bl\-Rep\-One\-S\-Chain}}

\subsubsection[{bl\-Rep\-One\-S\-Chain}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf B\-O\-O\-L} bl\-Rep\-One\-S\-Chain (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf P\-D\-B} $\ast$}]{pdb, }
\item[{char $\ast$}]{Res\-Spec, }
\item[{char}]{aa, }
\item[{char $\ast$}]{Chi\-Table, }
\item[{char $\ast$}]{Ref\-Coords}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}\label{pdb_8h_af900f21c1a37ba63496962ab1ffec576}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\tt in,out}  & {\em $\ast$pdb} & P\-D\-B linked list to modify \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$\-Res\-Spec} & Residue spec for residue to replace in the format \mbox{[}c\mbox{]}nnn\mbox{[}i\mbox{]} \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em aa} & The 1-\/letter code for the new sidechain \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$\-Chi\-Table} & The equivalent Chi table \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$\-Ref\-Coords} & The reference coordinates file \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Success?
\end{DoxyReturn}
Replace a single sidechain. Takes a P\-D\-B linked list, a residues specfication (in the form \mbox{[}c\mbox{]}nnn\mbox{[}i\mbox{]} where \mbox{[}c\mbox{]} is an optional chain name, nnn is a residue number and \mbox{[}i\mbox{]} is an optional insert code) and a 1-\/letter code of the required sidechain and does a simple maximum overlap replacement of the sidechain. Also requires filenames of the two datafiles.

Replace a single sidechain. Takes a P\-D\-B linked list, a residues specfication (in the form \mbox{[}c\mbox{]}nnn\mbox{[}i\mbox{]} where \mbox{[}c\mbox{]} is an optional chain name, nnn is a residue number and \mbox{[}i\mbox{]} is an optional insert code) and a 1-\/letter code of the required sidechain and does a simple maximum overlap replacement of the sidechain. Also requires filenames of the two datafiles.

Replaces even if the sidechain was coorect already

\hypertarget{pdb_8h_ab6752fd043cf86fcc57fef437f68f758}{\index{pdb.\-h@{pdb.\-h}!bl\-Select\-Atoms\-P\-D\-B\-As\-Copy@{bl\-Select\-Atoms\-P\-D\-B\-As\-Copy}}
\index{bl\-Select\-Atoms\-P\-D\-B\-As\-Copy@{bl\-Select\-Atoms\-P\-D\-B\-As\-Copy}!pdb.h@{pdb.\-h}}
\subsubsection[{bl\-Select\-Atoms\-P\-D\-B\-As\-Copy}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf P\-D\-B}$\ast$ bl\-Select\-Atoms\-P\-D\-B\-As\-Copy (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf P\-D\-B} $\ast$}]{pdbin, }
\item[{int}]{nsel, }
\item[{char $\ast$$\ast$}]{sel, }
\item[{int $\ast$}]{natom}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}\label{pdb_8h_ab6752fd043cf86fcc57fef437f68f758}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$pdbin} & Input list \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em nsel} & Number of atom types to keep \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$$\ast$sel} & List of atom types to keep \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt out}  & {\em $\ast$natom} & Number of atoms kept \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Output list
\end{DoxyReturn}
Take a P\-D\-B linked list and returns a list containing only those atom types specified in the sel array.

To set up the list of atoms to keep, define an array of pointers to char\-: e.\-g. char $\ast$sel\mbox{[}10\mbox{]} Then define the atoms in the list thus\-:

\begin{DoxyVerb}        SELECT(sel[0],"N   ");
        SELECT(sel[1],"CA  ");
        SELECT(sel[2],"C   ");
        SELECT(sel[3],"O   ");
\end{DoxyVerb}


Ensure the spaces are used!!

N.\-B. The routine is non-\/destructive; i.\-e. the original P\-D\-B linked list is intact after the selection process

\hypertarget{pdb_8h_a803184a2bdeaf7ba9096dab94a479bbd}{\index{pdb.\-h@{pdb.\-h}!bl\-Select\-Ca\-P\-D\-B@{bl\-Select\-Ca\-P\-D\-B}}
\index{bl\-Select\-Ca\-P\-D\-B@{bl\-Select\-Ca\-P\-D\-B}!pdb.h@{pdb.\-h}}
\subsubsection[{bl\-Select\-Ca\-P\-D\-B}]{\setlength{\rightskip}{0pt plus 5cm}{\bf P\-D\-B}$\ast$ bl\-Select\-Ca\-P\-D\-B (
\begin{DoxyParamCaption}
\item[{{\bf P\-D\-B} $\ast$}]{pdb}
\end{DoxyParamCaption}
)}}\label{pdb_8h_a803184a2bdeaf7ba9096dab94a479bbd}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$pdb} & A P\-D\-B linked list \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt out}  & {\em $\ast$} & The linked list reduced to C\-A atoms only\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
Reduce a P\-D\-B linked list to C\-A atoms only. Returns the reduced P\-D\-B linked list. Note that the input linked list is modified (storage for non-\/\-C\-A atoms is freed) and that the pointer input to the routine is likely to become invalid since the first atom is generally no a C\-A and the first record will therefore be freed.

Normally you would call this routine with something like\-:

pdb = Select\-Ca\-P\-D\-B(pdb);

i.\-e. the same variable name is used for the input and the return.

This is used in place of the normal Select\-Atoms\-P\-D\-B() since it is simpler and faster to call for this rather common requirement.

N.\-B. Unlike Select\-Atoms\-P\-D\-B(), the routine is destructive; i.\-e. the original P\-D\-B linked list is N\-O\-T intact after the selection process.

\item 15.\-10.\-96 Original By\-: A\-C\-R\-M
\item 11.\-01.\-02 Added check on pdb!=N\-U\-L\-L in case there are no C\-As (D\-N\-A etc)
\item 07.\-07.\-14 Use bl prefix for functions By\-: C\-T\-P 
\end{DoxyItemize}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\tt in,out}  & {\em $\ast$pdb} & P\-D\-B linked list to change \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em $\ast$next} & If N\-U\-L\-L, move all atoms in the linked list from the last atom in the torsion. Otherwise move atoms up to (but not including) next. Normally this would be the start of the next residue. \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em chi} & Sidechain chi angle to set \\
\hline
\mbox{\tt in}  & {\em type} & Torsion angle to set (as defined below)\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
Sets a sidechain torsion angle in a pdb linked list. The routine assumes standard atom ordering\-: N,C\-A,C,O,s/c with standard order in the s/c.

The type input parameter is defined as follows\-:

\begin{DoxyVerb}     type     Atom names        Sequential atom numbers
     --------------------------------------------------
     0        N,  CA, CB, XG    (0 - 1 - 4 - 5)
     1        CA, CB, XG, XD    (1 - 4 - 5 - 6)
     2        CB, XG, XD, XE    (4 - 5 - 6 - 7)
     3        XG, XD, XE, XZ    (5 - 6 - 7 - 8)
\end{DoxyVerb}

Removes all Glycine C\-B pseudo-\/atoms added by Add\-Gly\-C\-B() The linked list is modified in-\/place, but the return value should be used in case the very first item in the linked list is a Gly-\/\-C\-B which will be removed by the code.

Skips\-: R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 500 D\-B\-R\-E\-F H\-E\-L\-I\-X S\-H\-E\-E\-T S\-S\-B\-O\-N\-D C\-I\-S\-P\-E\-P S\-E\-Q\-A\-D\-V M\-O\-D\-R\-E\-S H\-E\-T S\-I\-T\-E R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 465 R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 470 R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 475 R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 480 R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 525 R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 610 R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 615 R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 620 R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 630 R\-E\-M\-A\-R\-K 3
